  [user_task_description] # ContentPublishingHub Web Application Specification  ## Objective Build a comprehensive content management system with version control, content scheduling, and analytics. The system supports collaborative content creation with version history tracking, editorial comments, and content analytics. Testing should start from the Dashboard page.  ## Language Python (Flask framework recommended)  ## Page Design  ### 1. Dashboard Page (`dashboard.html`) **Route:** `/dashboard` **Purpose:** Main landing page showing content overview and navigation **Elements:** - Page container (id: `dashboard-page`) - Welcome message with username (id: `welcome-message`) - Quick stats section (id: `quick-stats`) - Create Article button (id: `create-article-button`) - Recent activity feed (id: `recent-activity`)  ### 2. Create Article Page (`create_article.html`) **Route:** `/article/create` **Purpose:** Editor for creating new articles **Elements:** - Page container (id: `create-article-page`) - Article title input (id: `article-title`) - Content editor textarea (id: `article-content`) - Save as Draft button (id: `save-draft-button`) - Cancel button (id: `cancel-button`)  ### 3. Edit Article Page (`edit_article.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/edit` **Purpose:** Edit existing article with version tracking **Elements:** - Page container (id: `edit-article-page`) - Article title input (id: `edit-article-title`) - Content editor textarea (id: `edit-article-content`) - Save New Version button (id: `save-version-button`) - Cancel button (id: `cancel-edit`)  ### 4. Article Version History Page (`version_history.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/versions` **Purpose:** View all versions and restore previous versions **Elements:** - Page container (id: `version-history-page`) - Versions list (id: `versions-list`) - Version comparison section (id: `version-comparison`) - Restore button (id: `restore-version-1`) - Back to Edit button (id: `back-to-edit-history`)  ### 5. My Articles Page (`my_articles.html`) **Route:** `/articles/mine` **Purpose:** List user's articles with filters **Elements:** - Page container (id: `my-articles-page`) - Filter by status dropdown (id: `filter-article-status`) - Articles table (id: `articles-table`) - Create New Article button (id: `create-new-article`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard`)  ### 6. Published Articles Page (`published_articles.html`) **Route:** `/articles/published` **Purpose:** Public-facing content library **Elements:** - Page container (id: `published-articles-page`) - Filter by category dropdown (id: `filter-published-category`) - Articles grid (id: `published-articles-grid`) - Sort by dropdown (id: `sort-published`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-published`)  ### 7. Content Calendar Page (`content_calendar.html`) **Route:** `/calendar` **Purpose:** Scheduled publications timeline view **Elements:** - Page container (id: `calendar-page`) - Calendar view selector (id: `calendar-view`) - Calendar grid (id: `calendar-grid`) - Schedule button (id: `schedule-button`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-calendar`)  ### 8. Article Analytics Page (`article_analytics.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/analytics` **Purpose:** View engagement metrics for published article **Elements:** - Page container (id: `analytics-page`) - Analytics overview (id: `analytics-overview`) - Total views (id: `analytics-total-views`) - Unique visitors (id: `analytics-unique-visitors`) - Back to Article button (id: `back-to-article-analytics`)  ## Data Storage  The 'ContentPublishingHub' application will store data locally in text files organized in the directory 'data'. The following data formats and examples are defined:  ### 1. users.txt Format: `username|email|fullname|created_date` Example: ``` john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15 alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16 bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17 admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10 ```  ### 2. articles.txt Format: `article_id|title|author|category|status|tags|featured_image|meta_description|created_date|publish_date` Example: ``` 1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00 2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00 3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24| ``` status: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived category: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release  ### 3. article_versions.txt Format: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary` Example: ``` 1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft 2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction 3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version ```  ### 4. approvals.txt Format: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp` Example: ``` 1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00 2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00 3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00 ``` status: approved, rejected, revision_requested  ### 5. workflow_stages.txt Format: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required` Example: ``` 1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes 2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes 3|news|Editor Review|1|yes 4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes 5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes ```  ### 6. comments.txt Format: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp` Example: ``` 1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00 2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00 3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00 ```  ### 7. analytics.txt Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares` Example: ``` 1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12 2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18 3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15 4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8 ```

Dashboard Page (`dashboard.html`)\n- Page container: `<div id=\"dashboard-page\">`\n- Welcome message: `<div id=\"welcome-message\">` displays \"Welcome, {username}!\"\n- Quick stats section: `<section id=\"quick-stats\">`\n- Create Article button: `<button id=\"create-article-button\">Create Article</button>`\n- Recent activity feed: `<div id=\"recent-activity\">` List recent content actions\n\n### 2. Create Article Page (`create_article.html`)\n- Page container: `<div id=\"create-article-page\">`\n- Article title input: `<input type=\"text\" id=\"article-title\" name=\"article_title\">`\n- Content editor textarea: `<textarea id=\"article-content\" name=\"article_content\"></textarea>`\n- Save as Draft button: `<button id=\"save-draft-button\">Save as Draft</button>`\n- Cancel button: `<button id=\"cancel-button\">Cancel</button>`\n\n### 3. Edit Article Page (`edit_article.html`)\n- Page container: `<div id=\"edit-article-page\">`\n- Article title input: `<input type=\"text\" id=\"edit-article-title\" name=\"edit_article_title\" value=\"{{ title }}\">`\n- Content editor textarea: `<textarea id=\"edit-article-content\" name=\"edit_article_content\">{{ content }}</textarea>`\n- Save New Version button: `<button id=\"save-version-button\">Save New Version</button>`\n- Cancel button: `<button id=\"cancel-edit\">Cancel</button>`\n\n### 4. Article Version History Page (`version_history.html`)\n- Page container: `<div id=\"version-history-page\">`\n- Versions list: `<ul id=\"versions-list\">` with each version listed (version number, date, change summary)\n- Version comparison section: `<div id=\"version-comparison\">` to show diff between versions\n- Restore button: `<button id=\"restore-version-1\">Restore Selected Version</button>`\n- Back to Edit button: `<button id=\"back-to-edit-history\">Back to Edit</button>`\n\n### 5. My Articles Page (`my_articles.html`)\n- Page container: `<div id=\"my-articles-page\">`\n- Filter by status dropdown: `<select id=\"filter-article-status\">` with options: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived\n- Articles table: `<table id=\"articles-table\">` with columns for Title, Category, Status, Publish Date, Actions\n- Create New Article button: `<button id=\"create-new-article\">Create New Article</button>`\n- Back to Dashboard button: `<button id=\"back-to-dashboard\">Back to Dashboard</button>`\n\n### 6. Published Articles Page (`published_articles.html`)\n- Page container: `<div id=\"published-articles-page\">`\n- Filter by category dropdown: `<select id=\"filter-published-category\">` with options: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release\n- Articles grid: `<div id=\"published-articles-grid\">` shows article previews (title, image, publish date)\n- Sort by dropdown: `<select id=\"sort-published\">` with options like publish_date ascending/descending\n- Back to Dashboard button: `<button id=\"back-to-dashboard-published\">Back to Dashboard</button>`\n\n### 7. Content Calendar Page (`content_calendar.html`)\n- Page container: `<div id=\"calendar-page\">`\n- Calendar view selector: `<select id=\"calendar-view\">` options: daily, weekly, monthly\n- Calendar grid: `<div id=\"calendar-grid\">` displays scheduled articles by date\n- Schedule button: `<button id=\"schedule-button\">Schedule</button>`\n- Back to Dashboard button: `<button id=\"back-to-dashboard-calendar\">Back to Dashboard</button>`\n\n### 8. Article Analytics Page (`article_analytics.html`)\n- Page container: `<div id=\"analytics-page\">`\n- Analytics overview: `<section id=\"analytics-overview\">`\n- Total views: `<span id=\"analytics-total-views\">`\n- Unique visitors: `<span id=\"analytics-unique-visitors\">`\n- Back to Article button: `<button id=\"back-to-article-analytics\">Back to Article</button>`\n\n---\n\n## Section 3: Data File Schemas\n\n### 1. users.txt\n- Format: `username|email|fullname|created_date`\n- Fields:\n  1. username (str) - unique user identifier\n  2. email (str) - user email address\n  3. fullname (str) - full name of user\n  4. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date user account was created\n- Example:\n```\njohn|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15\nalice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16\nbob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17\nadmin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10\n```\n\n### 2. articles.txt\n- Format: `article_id|title|author|category|status|tags|featured_image|meta_description|created_date|publish_date`\n- Fields:\n  1. article_id (int) - unique article identifier\n  2. title (str) - article title\n  3. author (str) - username of author\n  4. category (enum) - one of: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release\n  5. status (enum) - one of: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived\n  6. tags (csv) - comma-separated list of tags\n  7. featured_image (str) - path/URL to the featured image (nullable)\n  8. meta_description (str) - brief description\n  9. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date created\n  10. publish_date (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - date/time published (nullable)\n- Example:\n```\n1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00\n2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00\n3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24|\n```\n\n### 3. article_versions.txt\n- Format: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary`\n- Fields:\n  1. version_id (int) - unique version identifier\n  2. article_id (int) - associated article\n  3. version_number (int) - numeric version number\n  4. content (str) - article content text\n  5. author (str) - username who made the change\n  6. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - version creation timestamp\n  7. change_summary (str) - brief description of changes\n- Example:\n```\n1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft\n2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction\n3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version\n```\n\n### 4. approvals.txt\n- Format: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp`\n- Fields:\n  1. approval_id (int) - unique approval record\n  2. article_id (int) - article related\n  3. version_id (int) - version approved/rejected\n  4. approver (str) - username of approver\n  5. status (enum) - approved, rejected, revision_requested\n  6. comments (str) - approver comments\n  7. timestamp (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - approval timestamp\n- Example:\n```\n1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00\n2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00\n3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00\n```\n\n### 5. workflow_stages.txt\n- Format: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required`\n- Fields:\n  1. stage_id (int) - unique workflow stage\n  2. category (str) - article category\n  3. stage_name (str) - name of the workflow step\n  4. stage_order (int) - numeric order of the stage\n  5. is_required (str) - \"yes\" or \"no\" indicating if mandatory\n- Example:\n```\n1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes\n2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes\n3|news|Editor Review|1|yes\n4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes\n5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes\n```\n\n### 6. comments.txt\n- Format: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp`\n- Fields:\n  1. comment_id (int) - unique comment identifier\n  2. article_id (int) - article related\n  3. version_id (int) - version related\n  4. user (str) - username who commented\n  5. comment_text (str) - comment content\n  6. timestamp (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - comment timestamp\n- Example:\n```\n1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00\n2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00\n3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00\n```\n\n### 7. analytics.txt\n- Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares`\n- Fields:\n  1. analytics_id (int) - unique analytics record\n  2. article_id (int) - article referenced\n  3. date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date of analytics\n  4. views (int) - total views\n  5. unique_visitors (int) - unique visitors\n  6. avg_time_seconds (int) - average time spent in seconds\n  7. shares (int) - number of times shared\n- Example:\n```\n1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12\n2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18\n3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15\n4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8\n```\n\n---\n\n*This design specification document enables the backend and frontend teams to implement the 'ContentPublishingHub' application independently and in alignment with all specified requirements.*\n"})

Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00 2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00 3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00 ```  ### 7. analytics.txt Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares` Example: ``` 1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12 2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18 3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15 4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8 ```
  [design_spec.md] # ContentPublishingHub Design Specification  ---  ## Section 1: Flask Routes Specification  | Route Pattern                      | Methods  | Function Name                  | Template Rendered       | Context Variables                             | |----------------------------------|----------|-------------------------------|------------------------|-----------------------------------------------| | `/dashboard`                     | GET      | dashboard                     | dashboard.html         | `username` (str), `quick_stats` (dict), `recent_activity` (list of dicts) | | `/article/create`                | GET, POST| create_article                | create_article.html    | GET: None; POST: result messages or validation errors | | `/article/<article_id>/edit`    | GET, POST| edit_article                  | edit_article.html      | `article_id` (int), `title` (str), `content` (str) | | `/article/<article_id>/versions`| GET      | article_version_history       | version_history.html   | `article_id` (int), `versions` (list of dicts), `comparison` (dict), `current_version` (int) | | `/articles/mine`                | GET      | my_articles                   | my_articles.html       | `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_status` (str) | | `/articles/published`           | GET      | published_articles            | published_articles.html| `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_category` (str), `sort_option` (str) | | `/calendar`                    | GET, POST| content_calendar              | content_calendar.html  | `calendar_view` (str), `calendar_data` (list or dict of scheduled articles) | | `/article/<article_id>/analytics`| GET    | article_analytics             | article_analytics.html | `article_id` (int), `analytics` (dict) |  ---  ## Section 2: HTML Template Structure  ### 1. Dashboard Page (`dashboard.html`) - Page container: `<div id="dashboard-page">` - Welcome message: `<div id="welcome-message">` displays "Welcome, {username}!" - Quick stats section: `<section id="quick-stats">` - Create Article button: `<button id="create-article-button">Create Article</button>` - Recent activity feed: `<div id="recent-activity">` List recent content actions  ### 2. Create Article Page (`create_article.html`) - Page container: `<div id="create-article-page">` - Article title input: `<input type="text" id="article-title" name="article_title">` - Content editor textarea: `<textarea id="article-content" name="article_content"></textarea>` - Save as Draft button: `<button id="save-draft-button">Save as Draft</button>` - Cancel button: `<button id="cancel-button">Cancel</button>`  ### 3. Edit Article Page (`edit_article.html`) - Page container: `<div id="edit-article-page">` - Article title input: `<input type="text" id="edit-article-title" name="edit_article_title" value="{{ title }}">` - Content editor textarea: `<textarea id="edit-article-content" name="edit_article_content">{{ content }}</textarea>` - Save New Version button: `<button id="save-version-button">Save New Version</button>` - Cancel button: `<button id="cancel-edit">Cancel</button>`  ### 4. Article Version History Page (`version_history.html`) - Page container: `<div id="version-history-page">` - Versions list: `<ul id="versions-list">` with each version listed (version number, date, change summary) - Version comparison section: `<div id="version-comparison">` to show diff between versions - Restore button: `<button id="restore-version-1">Restore Selected Version</button>` - Back to Edit button: `<button id="back-to-edit-history">Back to Edit</button>`  ### 5. My Articles Page (`my_articles.html`) - Page container: `<div id="my-articles-page">` - Filter by status dropdown: `<select id="filter-article-status">` with options: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived - Articles table: `<table id="articles-table">` with columns for Title, Category, Status, Publish Date, Actions - Create New Article button: `<button id="create-new-article">Create New Article</button>` - Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard">Back to Dashboard</button>`  ### 6. Published Articles Page (`published_articles.html`) - Page container: `<div id="published-articles-page">` - Filter by category dropdown: `<select id="filter-published-category">` with options: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release - Articles grid: `<div id="published-articles-grid">` shows article previews (title, image, publish date) - Sort by dropdown: `<select id="sort-published">` with options like publish_date ascending/descending - Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard-published">Back to Dashboard</button>`  ### 7. Article Analytics Page (`article_analytics.html`) - Page container: `<div id="analytics-page">` - Analytics overview: `<section id="analytics-overview">` - Total views: `<span id="analytics-total-views">` - Unique visitors: `<span id="analytics-unique-visitors">` - Back to Article button: `<button id="back-to-article-analytics">Back to Article</button>`  ---  ## Section 3: Data File Schemas  ### 1. users.txt - Format: `username|email|fullname|created_date` - Fields:   1. username (str) - unique user identifier   2. email (str) - user email address   3. fullname (str) - full name of user   4. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date user account was created - Example: ``` john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15 alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16 bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17 admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10 ```  ### 2. articles.txt - Format: `article_id|title|author|category|status|tags|featured_image|meta_description|created_date|publish_date` - Fields:   1. article_id (int) - unique article identifier   2. title (str) - article title   3. author (str) - username of author   4. category (enum) - one of: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release   5. status (enum) - one of: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived   6. tags (csv) - comma-separated list of tags   7. featured_image (str) - path/URL to the featured image (nullable)   8. meta_description (str) - brief description   9. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date created   10. publish_date (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - date/time published (nullable) - Example: ``` 1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00 2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00 3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24| ```  ### 3. article_versions.txt - Format: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary` - Fields:   1. version_id (int) - unique version identifier   2. article_id (int) - associated article   3. version_number (int) - numeric version number   4. content (str) - article content text   5. author (str) - username who made the change   6. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - version creation timestamp   7. change_summary (str) - brief description of changes - Example: ``` 1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft 2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction 3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version ```  ### 4. approvals.txt - Format: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp` - Fields:   1. approval_id (int) - unique approval record   2. article_id (int) - article related   3. version_id (int) - version approved/rejected   4. approver (str) - username of approver   5. status (enum) - approved, rejected, revision_requested   6. comments (str) - approver comments   7. timestamp (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - approval timestamp - Example: ``` 1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00 2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00 3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00 ```  ### 5. workflow_stages.txt - Format: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required` - Fields:   1. stage_id (int) - unique workflow stage   2. category (str) - article category   3. stage_name (str) - name of the workflow step   4. stage_order (int) - numeric order of the stage   5. is_required (str) - "yes" or "no" indicating if mandatory - Example: ``` 1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes 2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes 3|news|Editor Review|1|yes 4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes 5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes ```  ### 6. comments.txt - Format: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp` - Fields:   1. comment_id (int) - unique comment identifier   2. article_id (int) - article related   3. version_id (int) - version related   4. user (str) - username who commented   5. comment_text (str) - comment content   6. timestamp (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - comment timestamp - Example: ``` 1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00 2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00 3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00 ```  ### 7. analytics.txt - Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares` - Fields:   1. analytics_id (int) - unique analytics record   2. article_id (int) - article referenced   3. date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date of analytics   4. views (int) - total views   5. unique_visitors (int) - unique visitors   6. avg_time_seconds (int) - average time spent in seconds   7. shares (int) - number of times shared - Example: ``` 1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12 2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18 3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15 4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8 ```  ---  *This design specification document enables the backend and frontend teams to implement the 'ContentPublishingHub' application independently and in alignment with all specified requirements.*
================================================================================

# ContentPublishingHub Web Application Specification

## Objective
Build a comprehensive content management system with version control, content scheduling, and analytics. The system supports collaborative content creation with version history tracking, editorial comments, and content analytics. Testing should start from the Dashboard page.

## Language
Python (Flask framework recommended)

## Page Design

### 1. Dashboard Page (`dashboard.html`)
**Route:** `/dashboard`
**Purpose:** Main landing page showing content overview and navigation
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `dashboard-page`)
- Welcome message with username (id: `welcome-message`)
- Quick stats section (id: `quick-stats`)
- Create Article button (id: `create-article-button`)
- Recent activity feed (id: `recent-activity`)

### 2. Create Article Page (`create_article.html`)
**Route:** `/article/create`
**Purpose:** Editor for creating new articles
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `create-article-page`)
- Article title input (id: `article-title`)
- Content editor textarea (id: `article-content`)
- Save as Draft button (id: `save-draft-button`)
- Cancel button (id: `cancel-button`)

### 3. Edit Article Page (`edit_article.html`)
**Route:** `/article/<article_id>/edit`
**Purpose:** Edit existing article with version tracking
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `edit-article-page`)
- Article title input (id: `edit-article-title`)
- Content editor textarea (id: `edit-article-content`)
- Save New Version button (id: `save-version-button`)
- Cancel button (id: `cancel-edit`)

### 4. Article Version History Page (`version_history.html`)
**Route:** `/article/<article_id>/versions`
**Purpose:** View all versions and restore previous versions
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `version-history-page`)
- Versions list (id: `versions-list`)
- Version comparison section (id: `version-comparison`)
- Restore button (id: `restore-version-1`)
- Back to Edit button (id: `back-to-edit-history`)

### 5. My Articles Page (`my_articles.html`)
**Route:** `/articles/mine`
**Purpose:** List user's articles with filters
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `my-articles-page`)
- Filter by status dropdown (id: `filter-article-status`)
- Articles table (id: `articles-table`)
- Create New Article button (id: `create-new-article`)
- Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard`)

### 6. Published Articles Page (`published_articles.html`)
**Route:** `/articles/published`
**Purpose:** Public-facing content library
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `published-articles-page`)
- Filter by category dropdown (id: `filter-published-category`)
- Articles grid (id: `published-articles-grid`)
- Sort by dropdown (id: `sort-published`)
- Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-published`)

### 7. Content Calendar Page (`content_calendar.html`)
**Route:** `/calendar`
**Purpose:** Scheduled publications timeline view
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `calendar-page`)
- Calendar view selector (id: `calendar-view`)
- Calendar grid (id: `calendar-grid`)
- Schedule button (id: `schedule-button`)
- Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-calendar`)

### 8. Article Analytics Page (`article_analytics.html`)
**Route:** `/article/<article_id>/analytics`
**Purpose:** View engagement metrics for published article
**Elements:**
- Page container (id: `analytics-page`)
- Analytics overview (id: `analytics-overview`)
- Total views (id: `analytics-total-views`)
- Unique visitors (id: `analytics-unique-visitors`)
- Back to Article button (id: `back-to-article-analytics`)

## Data Storage

The 'ContentPublishingHub' application will store data locally in text files organized in the directory 'data'. The following data formats and examples are defined:

### 1. users.txt
Format: `username|email|fullname|created_date`
Example:
```
john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15
alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16
bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17
admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10
```

### 2. articles.txt
Format: `article_id|title|author|category|status|tags|featured_image|meta_description|created_date|publish_date`
Example:
```
1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00
2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00
3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24|
```
status: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived
category: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release

### 3. article_versions.txt
Format: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary`
Example:
```
1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft
2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction
3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version
```

### 4. approvals.txt
Format: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp`
Example:
```
1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00
2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00
3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00
```
status: approved, rejected, revision_requested

### 5. workflow_stages.txt
Format: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required`
Example:
```
1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes
2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes
3|news|Editor Review|1|yes
4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes
5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes
```

### 6. comments.txt
Format: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp`
Example:
```
1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00
2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00
3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00
```

### 7. analytics.txt
Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares`
Example:
```
1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12
2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18
3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15
4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8
```


=== design_spec.md ===
# ContentPublishingHub Design Specification

---

## Section 1: Flask Routes Specification

| Route Pattern                      | Methods  | Function Name                  | Template Rendered       | Context Variables                             |
|----------------------------------|----------|-------------------------------|------------------------|-----------------------------------------------|
| `/dashboard`                     | GET      | dashboard                     | dashboard.html         | `username` (str), `quick_stats` (dict), `recent_activity` (list of dicts) |
| `/article/create`                | GET, POST| create_article                | create_article.html    | GET: None; POST: result messages or validation errors |
| `/article/<article_id>/edit`    | GET, POST| edit_article                  | edit_article.html      | `article_id` (int), `title` (str), `content` (str) |
| `/article/<article_id>/versions`| GET      | article_version_history       | version_history.html   | `article_id` (int), `versions` (list of dicts), `comparison` (dict), `current_version` (int) |
| `/articles/mine`                | GET      | my_articles                   | my_articles.html       | `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_status` (str) |
| `/articles/published`           | GET      | published_articles            | published_articles.html| `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_category` (str), `sort_option` (str) |
| `/calendar`                    | GET, POST| content_calendar              | content_calendar.html  | `calendar_view` (str), `calendar_data` (list or dict of scheduled articles) |
| `/article/<article_id>/analytics`| GET    | article_analytics             | article_analytics.html | `article_id` (int), `analytics` (dict) |

---

## Section 2: HTML Template Structure

### 1. Dashboard Page (`dashboard.html`)
- Page container: `<div id="dashboard-page">`
- Welcome message: `<div id="welcome-message">` displays "Welcome, {username}!"
- Quick stats section: `<section id="quick-stats">`
- Create Article button: `<button id="create-article-button">Create Article</button>`
- Recent activity feed: `<div id="recent-activity">` List recent content actions

### 2. Create Article Page (`create_article.html`)
- Page container: `<div id="create-article-page">`
- Article title input: `<input type="text" id="article-title" name="article_title">`
- Content editor textarea: `<textarea id="article-content" name="article_content"></textarea>`
- Save as Draft button: `<button id="save-draft-button">Save as Draft</button>`
- Cancel button: `<button id="cancel-button">Cancel</button>`

### 3. Edit Article Page (`edit_article.html`)
- Page container: `<div id="edit-article-page">`
- Article title input: `<input type="text" id="edit-article-title" name="edit_article_title" value="{{ title }}">`
- Content editor textarea: `<textarea id="edit-article-content" name="edit_article_content">{{ content }}</textarea>`
- Save New Version button: `<button id="save-version-button">Save New Version</button>`
- Cancel button: `<button id="cancel-edit">Cancel</button>`

### 4. Article Version History Page (`version_history.html`)

- Version comparison section: `<div id="version-comparison">` to show diff between versions
- Restore button: `<button id="restore-version-1">Restore Selected Version</button>`
- Back to Edit button: `<button id="back-to-edit-history">Back to Edit</button>`

### 5. My Articles Page (`my_articles.html`)
- Page container: `<div id="my-articles-page">`
- Filter by status dropdown: `<select id="filter-article-status">` with options: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived
- Articles table: `<table id="articles-table">` with columns for Title, Category, Status, Publish Date, Actions
- Create New Article button: `<button id="create-new-article">Create New Article</button>`
- Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard">Back to Dashboard</button>`

### 6. Published Articles Page (`published_articles.html`)
- Page container: `<div id="published-articles-page">`
- Filter by category dropdown: `<select id="filter-published-category">` with options: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release
- Articles grid: `<div id="published-articles-grid">` shows article previews (title, image, publish date)
- Sort by dropdown: `<select id="sort-published">` with options like publish_date ascending/descending
- Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard-published">Back to Dashboard</button>`

### 7. Content Calendar Page (`content_calendar.html`)
- Page container: `<div id="calendar-page">`
- Calendar view selector: `<select id="calendar-view">` options: daily, weekly, monthly
- Calendar grid: `<div id="calendar-grid">` displays scheduled articles by date
- Schedule button: `<button id="schedule-button">Schedule</button>`
- Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard-calendar">Back to Dashboard</button>`

### 8. Article Analytics Page (`article_analytics.html`)
- Page container: `<div id="analytics-page">`
- Analytics overview: `<section id="analytics-overview">`
- Total views: `<span id="analytics-total-views">`
- Unique visitors: `<span id="analytics-unique-visitors">`
- Back to Article button: `<button id="back-to-article-analytics">Back to Article</button>`

---

## Section 3: Data File Schemas

### 1. users.txt
- Format: `username|email|fullname|created_date`
- Fields:
  1. username (str) - unique user identifier
  2. email (str) - user email address
  3. fullname (str) - full name of user
  4. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date user account was created
- Example:
```
john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15
alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16
bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17
admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10
```

### 2. articles.txt
- Format: `article_id|title|author|category|status|tags|featured_image|meta_description|created_date|publish_date`
- Fields:
  1. article_id (int) - unique article identifier
  2. title (str) - article title
  3. author (str) - username of author
  4. category (enum) - one of: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release
  5. status (enum) - one of: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived
  6. tags (csv) - comma-separated list of tags
  7. featured_image (str) - path/URL to the featured image (nullable)
  8. meta_description (str) - brief description
  9. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date created
  10. publish_date (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - date/time published (nullable)
- Example:
```
1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00
2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00
3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24|
```

### 3. article_versions.txt
- Format: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary`
- Fields:
  1. version_id (int) - unique version identifier
  2. article_id (int) - associated article
  3. version_number (int) - numeric version number
  4. content (str) - article content text
  5. author (str) - username who made the change
  6. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - version creation timestamp
  7. change_summary (str) - brief description of changes
- Example:
```
1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft
2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction
3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version
```

### 4. approvals.txt
- Format: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp`
- Fields:
  1. approval_id (int) - unique approval record
  2. article_id (int) - article related
  3. version_id (int) - version approved/rejected
  4. approver (str) - username of approver
  5. status (enum) - approved, rejected, revision_requested
  6. comments (str) - approver comments
  7. timestamp (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - approval timestamp
- Example:
```
1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00
2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00
3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00
```

### 5. workflow_stages.txt
- Format: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required`
- Fields:
  1. stage_id (int) - unique workflow stage
  2. category (str) - article category
  3. stage_name (str) - name of the workflow step
  4. stage_order (int) - numeric order of the stage
  5. is_required (str) - "yes" or "no" indicating if mandatory
- Example:
```
1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes
2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes
3|news|Editor Review|1|yes
4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes
5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes
```

### 6. comments.txt
- Format: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp`
- Fields:
  1. comment_id (int) - unique comment identifier
  2. article_id (int) - article related
  3. version_id (int) - version related
  4. user (str) - username who commented
  5. comment_text (str) - comment content
  6. timestamp (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - comment timestamp
- Example:
```
1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00
2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00
3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00
```

### 7. analytics.txt
- Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares`
- Fields:
  1. analytics_id (int) - unique analytics record
  2. article_id (int) - article referenced
  3. date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date of analytics
  4. views (int) - total views
  5. unique_visitors (int) - unique visitors
  6. avg_time_seconds (int) - average time spent in seconds
  7. shares (int) - number of times shared
- Example:
```
1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12
2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18
3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15
4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8
```

---

*This design specification document enables the backend and frontend teams to implement the 'ContentPublishingHub' application independently and in alignment with all specified requirements.*

[DEBUG] Review Content for RequirementsAnalyst -> FrontendDesigner:
  [user_task_description] # ContentPublishingHub Web Application Specification  ## Objective Build a comprehensive content management system with version control, content scheduling, and analytics. The system supports collaborative content creation with version history tracking, editorial comments, and content analytics. Testing should start from the Dashboard page.  ## Language Python (Flask framework recommended)  ## Page Design  ### 1. Dashboard Page (`dashboard.html`) **Route:** `/dashboard` **Purpose:** Main landing page showing content overview and navigation **Elements:** - Page container (id: `dashboard-page`) - Welcome message with username (id: `welcome-message`) - Quick stats section (id: `quick-stats`) - Create Article button (id: `create-article-button`) - Recent activity feed (id: `recent-activity`)  ### 2. Create Article Page (`create_article.html`) **Route:** `/article/create` **Purpose:** Editor for creating new articles **Elements:** - Page container (id: `create-article-page`) - Article title input (id: `article-title`) - Content editor textarea (id: `article-content`) - Save as Draft button (id: `save-draft-button`) - Cancel button (id: `cancel-button`)  ### 3. Edit Article Page (`edit_article.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/edit` **Purpose:** Edit existing article with version tracking **Elements:** - Page container (id: `edit-article-page`) - Article title input (id: `edit-article-title`) - Content editor textarea (id: `edit-article-content`) - Save New Version button (id: `save-version-button`) - Cancel button (id: `cancel-edit`)  ### 4. Article Version History Page (`version_history.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/versions` **Purpose:** View all versions and restore previous versions **Elements:** - Page container (id: `version-history-page`) - Versions list (id: `versions-list`) - Version comparison section (id: `version-comparison`) - Restore button (id: `restore-version-1`) - Back to Edit button (id: `back-to-edit-history`)  ### 5. My Articles Page (`my_articles.html`) **Route:** `/articles/mine` **Purpose:** List user's articles with filters **Elements:** - Page container (id: `my-articles-page`) - Filter by status dropdown (id: `filter-article-status`) - Articles table (id: `articles-table`) - Create New Article button (id: `create-new-article`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard`)  ### 6. Published Articles Page (`published_articles.html`) **Route:** `/articles/published` **Purpose:** Public-facing content library **Elements:** - Page container (id: `published-articles-page`) - Filter by category dropdown (id: `filter-published-category`) - Articles grid (id: `published-articles-grid`) - Sort by dropdown (id: `sort-published`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-published`)  ### 7. Content Calendar Page (`content_calendar.html`) **Route:** `/calendar` **Purpose:** Scheduled publications timeline view **Elements:** - Page container (id: `calendar-page`) - Calendar view selector (id: `calendar-view`) - Calendar grid (id: `calendar-grid`) - Schedule button (id: `schedule-button`) - Back to Dashboard button (id: `back-to-dashboard-calendar`)  ### 8. Article Analytics Page (`article_analytics.html`) **Route:** `/article/<article_id>/analytics` **Purpose:** View engagement metrics for published article **Elements:** - Page container (id: `analytics-page`) - Analytics overview (id: `analytics-overview`) - Total views (id: `analytics-total-views`) - Unique visitors (id: `analytics-unique-visitors`) - Back to Article button (id: `back-to-article-analytics`)  ## Data Storage  The 'ContentPublishingHub' application will store data locally in text files organized in the directory 'data'. The following data formats and examples are defined:  ### 1. users.txt Format: `username|email|fullname|created_date` Example: ``` john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15 alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16 bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17 admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10 ```  ### 2. articles.txt Format: `article_id|title|author|category|status|tags|featured_image|meta_description|created_date|publish_date` Example: ``` 1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00 2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00 3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24| ``` status: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived category: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release  ### 3. article_versions.txt Format: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary` Example: ``` 1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft 2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction 3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version ```  ### 4. approvals.txt Format: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp` Example: ``` 1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00 2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00 3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00 ``` status: approved, rejected, revision_requested  ### 5. workflow_stages.txt Format: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required` Example: ``` 1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes 2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes 3|news|Editor Review|1|yes 4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes 5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes ```  ### 6. comments.txt Format: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp` Example: ``` 1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00 2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00 3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00 ```  ### 7. analytics.txt Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares` Example: ``` 1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12 2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18 3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15 4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8 ```
  [design_spec.md] # ContentPublishingHub Design Specification  ---  ## Section 1: Flask Routes Specification  | Route Pattern                      | Methods  | Function Name                  | Template Rendered       | Context Variables                             | |----------------------------------|----------|-------------------------------|------------------------|-----------------------------------------------| | `/dashboard`                     | GET      | dashboard                     | dashboard.html         | `username` (str), `quick_stats` (dict), `recent_activity` (list of dicts) | | `/article/create`                | GET, POST| create_article                | create_article.html    | GET: None; POST: result messages or validation errors | | `/article/<article_id>/edit`    | GET, POST| edit_article                  | edit_article.html      | `article_id` (int), `title` (str), `content` (str) | | `/article/<article_id>/versions`| GET      | article_version_history       | version_history.html   | `article_id` (int), `versions` (list of dicts), `comparison` (dict), `current_version` (int) | | `/articles/mine`                | GET      | my_articles                   | my_articles.html       | `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_status` (str) | | `/articles/published`           | GET      | published_articles            | published_articles.html| `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_category` (str), `sort_option` (str) | | `/calendar`                    | GET, POST| content_calendar              | content_calendar.html  | `calendar_view` (str), `calendar_data` (list or dict of scheduled articles) | | `/article/<article_id>/analytics`| GET    | article_analytics             | article_analytics.html | `article_id` (int), `analytics` (dict) |  ---  ## Section 2: HTML Template Structure  ### 1. Dashboard Page (`dashboard.html`) - Page container: `<div id="dashboard-page">` - Welcome message: `<div id="welcome-message">` displays "Welcome, {username}!" - Quick stats section: `<section id="quick-stats">` - Create Article button: `<button id="create-article-button">Create Article</button>` - Recent activity feed: `<div id="recent-activity">` List recent content actions  ### 2. Create Article Page (`create_article.html`) - Page container: `<div id="create-article-page">` - Article title input: `<input type="text" id="article-title" name="article_title">` - Content editor textarea: `<textarea id="article-content" name="article_content"></textarea>` - Save as Draft button: `<button id="save-draft-button">Save as Draft</button>` - Cancel button: `<button id="cancel-button">Cancel</button>`  ### 3. Edit Article Page (`edit_article.html`) - Page container: `<div id="edit-article-page">` - Article title input: `<input type="text" id="edit-article-title" name="edit_article_title" value="{{ title }}">` - Content editor textarea: `<textarea id="edit-article-content" name="edit_article_content">{{ content }}</textarea>` - Save New Version button: `<button id="save-version-button">Save New Version</button>` - Cancel button: `<button id="cancel-edit">Cancel</button>`  ### 4. Article Version History Page (`version_history.html`) - Page container: `<div id="version-history-page">` - Versions list: `<ul id="versions-list">` with each version listed (version number, date, change summary) - Version comparison section: `<div id="version-comparison">` to show diff between versions - Restore button: `<button id="restore-version-1">Restore Selected Version</button>` - Back to Edit button: `<button id="back-to-edit-history">Back to Edit</button>`  ### 5. My Articles Page (`my_articles.html`) - Page container: `<div id="my-articles-page">` - Filter by status dropdown: `<select id="filter-article-status">` with options: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived - Articles table: `<table id="articles-table">` with columns for Title, Category, Status, Publish Date, Actions - Create New Article button: `<button id="create-new-article">Create New Article</button>` - Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard">Back to Dashboard</button>`  ### 6. Published Articles Page (`published_articles.html`) - Page container: `<div id="published-articles-page">` - Filter by category dropdown: `<select id="filter-published-category">` with options: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release - Articles grid: `<div id="published-articles-grid">` shows article previews (title, image, publish date) - Sort by dropdown: `<select id="sort-published">` with options like publish_date ascending/descending - Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard-published">Back to Dashboard</button>`  ### 7. Content Calendar Page (`content_calendar.html`) - Page container: `<div id="calendar-page">` - Calendar view selector: `<select id="calendar-view">` options: daily, weekly, monthly - Calendar grid: `<div id="calendar-grid">` displays scheduled articles by date - Schedule button: `<button id="schedule-button">Schedule</button>` - Back to Dashboard button: `<button id="back-to-dashboard-calendar">Back to Dashboard</button>`  ### 8. Article Analytics Page (`article_analytics.html`) - Page container: `<div id="analytics-page">` - Analytics overview: `<section id="analytics-overview">` - Total views: `<span id="analytics-total-views">` - Unique visitors: `<span id="analytics-unique-visitors">` - Back to Article button: `<button id="back-to-article-analytics">Back to Article</button>`  ---  ## Section 3: Data File Schemas  ### 1. users.txt - Format: `username|email|fullname|created_date` - Fields:   1. username (str) - unique user identifier   2. email (str) - user email address   3. fullname (str) - full name of user   4. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date user account was created - Example: ``` john|john@example.com|John Doe|2024-01-15 alice|alice@example.com|Alice Smith|2024-01-16 bob|bob@example.com|Bob Johnson|2024-01-17 admin|admin@example.com|Admin User|2024-01-10 ```  ### 2. articles.txt - Format: `article_id|title|author|category|status|tags|featured_image|meta_description|created_date|publish_date` - Fields:   1. article_id (int) - unique article identifier   2. title (str) - article title   3. author (str) - username of author   4. category (enum) - one of: news, blog, tutorial, announcement, press_release   5. status (enum) - one of: draft, pending_review, under_review, approved, published, rejected, archived   6. tags (csv) - comma-separated list of tags   7. featured_image (str) - path/URL to the featured image (nullable)   8. meta_description (str) - brief description   9. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date created   10. publish_date (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - date/time published (nullable) - Example: ``` 1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00 2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00 3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24| ```  ### 3. article_versions.txt - Format: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary` - Fields:   1. version_id (int) - unique version identifier   2. article_id (int) - associated article   3. version_number (int) - numeric version number   4. content (str) - article content text   5. author (str) - username who made the change   6. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - version creation timestamp   7. change_summary (str) - brief description of changes - Example: ``` 1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft 2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction 3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version ```  ### 4. approvals.txt - Format: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp` - Fields:   1. approval_id (int) - unique approval record   2. article_id (int) - article related   3. version_id (int) - version approved/rejected   4. approver (str) - username of approver   5. status (enum) - approved, rejected, revision_requested   6. comments (str) - approver comments   7. timestamp (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - approval timestamp - Example: ``` 1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00 2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00 3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00 ```  ### 5. workflow_stages.txt - Format: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required` - Fields:   1. stage_id (int) - unique workflow stage   2. category (str) - article category   3. stage_name (str) - name of the workflow step   4. stage_order (int) - numeric order of the stage   5. is_required (str) - "yes" or "no" indicating if mandatory - Example: ``` 1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes 2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes 3|news|Editor Review|1|yes 4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes 5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes ```  ### 6. comments.txt - Format: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp` - Fields:   1. comment_id (int) - unique comment identifier   2. article_id (int) - article related   3. version_id (int) - version related   4. user (str) - username who commented   5. comment_text (str) - comment content   6. timestamp (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - comment timestamp - Example: ``` 1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00 2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00 3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00 ```  ### 7. analytics.txt - Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares` - Fields:   1. analytics_id (int) - unique analytics record   2. article_id (int) - article referenced   3. date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date of analytics   4. views (int) - total views   5. unique_visitors (int) - unique visitors   6. avg_time_seconds (int) - average time spent in seconds   7. shares (int) - number of times shared - Example: ``` 1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12 2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18 3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15 4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8 ```  ---  *This design specification document enables the backend and frontend teams to implement the 'ContentPublishingHub' application independently and in alignment with all specified requirements.*

date/time published (nullable) - Example: ``` 1|Introduction to Flask|john|tutorial|published|python,flask,web|/img/flask.jpg|Learn Flask basics|2024-01-20|2024-01-22 10:00:00 2|Company Quarterly Update|alice|announcement|approved|company,news||Q1 results|2024-01-23|2024-01-25 09:00:00 3|New Product Launch|john|press_release|draft|product,launch|/img/product.jpg|Exciting new release|2024-01-24| ```  ### 3. article_versions.txt - Format: `version_id|article_id|version_number|content|author|created_date|change_summary` - Fields:   1. version_id (int) - unique version identifier   2. article_id (int) - associated article   3. version_number (int) - numeric version number   4. content (str) - article content text   5. author (str) - username who made the change   6. created_date (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - version creation timestamp   7. change_summary (str) - brief description of changes - Example: ``` 1|1|1|Flask is a micro web framework...|john|2024-01-20 14:30:00|Initial draft 2|1|2|Flask is a lightweight web framework...|john|2024-01-21 09:15:00|Improved introduction 3|2|1|We are pleased to announce...|alice|2024-01-23 11:00:00|Initial version ```  ### 4. approvals.txt - Format: `approval_id|article_id|version_id|approver|status|comments|timestamp` - Fields:   1. approval_id (int) - unique approval record   2. article_id (int) - article related   3. version_id (int) - version approved/rejected   4. approver (str) - username of approver   5. status (enum) - approved, rejected, revision_requested   6. comments (str) - approver comments   7. timestamp (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - approval timestamp - Example: ``` 1|1|2|alice|approved|Looks good, well written|2024-01-21 10:30:00 2|1|2|bob|approved|Ready for publication|2024-01-21 15:00:00 3|3|1|alice|rejected|Needs more details in section 2|2024-01-24 14:00:00 ```  ### 5. workflow_stages.txt - Format: `stage_id|category|stage_name|stage_order|is_required` - Fields:   1. stage_id (int) - unique workflow stage   2. category (str) - article category   3. stage_name (str) - name of the workflow step   4. stage_order (int) - numeric order of the stage   5. is_required (str) - "yes" or "no" indicating if mandatory - Example: ``` 1|tutorial|Editor Review|1|yes 2|tutorial|Publisher Approval|2|yes 3|news|Editor Review|1|yes 4|announcement|Editor Review|1|yes 5|announcement|Publisher Approval|2|yes ```  ### 6. comments.txt - Format: `comment_id|article_id|version_id|user|comment_text|timestamp` - Fields:   1. comment_id (int) - unique comment identifier   2. article_id (int) - article related   3. version_id (int) - version related   4. user (str) - username who commented   5. comment_text (str) - comment content   6. timestamp (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) - comment timestamp - Example: ``` 1|1|1|alice|Great start! Consider adding more examples.|2024-01-20 16:00:00 2|1|2|bob|The flow is much better now.|2024-01-21 11:00:00 3|3|1|alice|Section 2 needs expansion - add metrics.|2024-01-24 13:45:00 ```  ### 7. analytics.txt - Format: `analytics_id|article_id|date|views|unique_visitors|avg_time_seconds|shares` - Fields:   1. analytics_id (int) - unique analytics record   2. article_id (int) - article referenced   3. date (YYYY-MM-DD) - date of analytics   4. views (int) - total views   5. unique_visitors (int) - unique visitors   6. avg_time_seconds (int) - average time spent in seconds   7. shares (int) - number of times shared - Example: ``` 1|1|2024-01-22|150|120|245|12 2|1|2024-01-23|230|180|210|18 3|1|2024-01-24|180|140|220|15 4|2|2024-01-25|95|75|180|8 ```  ---  *This design specification document enables the backend and frontend teams to implement the 'ContentPublishingHub' application independently and in alignment with all specified requirements.*

Flask Application Structure\n\nThe Flask application for ContentPublishingHub will be organized into a modular and layered structure for maintainability, scalability, and clear separation of concerns:\n\n```\n/content_publishing_hub/\n|-- app.py                     # Flask application factory and app initialization\n|-- config.py                  # Configuration settings (environment, paths, etc.)\n|-- /controllers/              # Request handling and routing logic\n|    |-- dashboard.py\n|    |-- articles.py\n|    |-- calendar.py\n|    |-- analytics.py\n|    |-- __init__.py\n|-- /models/                   # Data access layer interacting with data/*.txt files\n|    |-- user_model.py\n|    |-- article_model.py\n|    |-- version_model.py\n|    |-- approval_model.py\n|    |-- comment_model.py\n|    |-- workflow_model.py\n|    |-- analytics_model.py\n|    |-- __init__.py\n|-- /services/                 # Business logic layer handling workflows, validation, versioning\n|    |-- article_service.py\n|    |-- versioning_service.py\n|    |-- approval_service.py\n|    |-- analytics_service.py\n|    |-- __init__.py\n|-- /utils/                    # Utility modules (file operations, version control management, helpers)\n|    |-- file_io.py            # Read/write for data/*.txt files\n|    |-- version_control.py    # Versioning logic (diff generation, history management)\n|    |-- validation.py\n|    |-- __init__.py\n|-- /templates/                # Frontend HTML templates (as per design_spec.md)\n|-- /static/                   # Static files: CSS, JS, Images\n|-- requirements.txt\n|-- README.md\n\n```\n\n### 2. Module Responsibilities\n\n- **app.py:** Entry point creating Flask app, registering blueprints from controllers, setting up config.\n- **controllers/**: Defines route handlers (e.g., dashboard, article creation/editing, version history, analytics).\n  - Each file targets related routes and coordinates input parsing, session handling, calling services, and response rendering.\n- **models/**: Manages reading/writing of raw persistent data stored in flat text files located under `data/` directory.\n  - Implements file parsing, data representation (e.g., users, articles, versions).\n  - Handles concurrency control if necessary when writing files.\n- **services/**: Implements business rules, workflows, version control, approval processing.\n  - Coordinates complex operations spanning multiple models.\n- **utils/file_io.py:** Provides robust abstractions for file access to read/write lines, parse to dicts, write back, ensuring data consistency.\n- **utils/version_control.py:** Manages version comparison, diff generation logic required for version history page.\n- **templates/**: HTML templates rendered by controllers passing the context variables.\n\n### 3. Data File Access and Management\n\n- All application data is persisted in the `data` folder as flat text files with `|` delimited fields.\n- Each model corresponds to a data file: `users.txt`, `articles.txt`, `article_versions.txt`, `approvals.txt`, `comments.txt`, `workflow_stages.txt`, `analytics.txt`.\n- Models provide methods such as `get_all()`, `get_by_id()`, `create()`, `update()`, and `filter()`.\n- On updating (e.g., adding new article version), models append new records to the respective files.\n- Read operations on these files are optimized in-memory caching if needed (optional based on scale), but always ensure fresh read on critical operations.\n\n### 4. Data Flow Between Components\n\n1. **Request Received:** Controller receives HTTP request.\n2. **Input Parsing:** Controller extracts parameters/query/form data.\n3. **Business Logic:** Controller calls services for operations like article creation, version management, approvals.\n4. **Data Access:** Services interact with models to read/write data files.\n5. **Response Preparation:** Services return data or status to controller.\n6. **Template Rendering:** Controller passes data context to frontend templates.\n7. **Response Sent:** Flask sends the rendered HTML or JSON response back to client.\n\n---\n\n## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints\n\nThe routing scheme aligns strictly with the design_spec.md routes and HTTP methods.\n\n| Route Pattern                      | Methods  | Controller Function           | Input                                    | Output/Context Variables                               |\n|----------------------------------|----------|------------------------------|-----------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------|\n| `/dashboard`                     | GET      | dashboard()                  | Session user info                         | `username`, `quick_stats` (dict), `recent_activity` (list of dicts) |\n| `/article/create`                | GET, POST| create_article()             | POST form: `article_title`, `article_content`         | On GET: None; On POST: success/error messages           |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/edit`| GET, POST| edit_article(article_id)     | URL param `article_id`, POST form: edited title & content | `article_id`, `title`, `content`                    |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/versions`| GET   | article_version_history(article_id) | URL param `article_id`                            | `article_id`, `versions` (list of dicts), `comparison` (dict), `current_version` (int) |\n| `/articles/mine`                | GET      | my_articles()                | Session user info, optional query filter status        | `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_status`              |\n| `/articles/published`           | GET      | published_articles()         | Optional query: `filter_category`, `sort_option`        | `articles` (list of dicts), `filter_category`, `sort_option`|\n| `/calendar`                    | GET, POST | content_calendar()           | POST form: calendar events or schedules                 | `calendar_view` (str), `calendar_data` (list or dict)     |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/analytics`| GET  | article_analytics(article_id) | URL param `article_id`                            | `article_id`, `analytics` (dict)                         |\n\n### Dynamic Routes\n\n- Routes like `/article/<article_id>/edit`, `/article/<article_id>/versions`, and `/article/<article_id>/analytics` use integer `article_id` URL path parameters.\n\n### User Sessions and Authentication\n\n- The system expects an authentication mechanism (e.g., login sessions) to provide `username` and user role context.\n- Controllers extract session user data to determine access rights (e.g., authors can edit their own articles).\n- Session management (login/logout) is assumed implemented but outside the scope of this document.\n\n---\n\n## Section 3: Version Control Design\n\n### 1. Article Versioning Model\n\n- Each article can have multiple versions tracked in `article_versions.txt`.\n- Version entries have `version_id`, `article_id`, `version_number`, `content`, `author`, `created_date`, and `change_summary`.\n- Version numbers increment sequentially per article.\n\n### 2. Version History and Comparison\n\n- The architecture supports retrieving all versions for an article.\n- Diff/Comparison logic implemented in `utils/version_control.py` generates changes summary for UI.\n- Users can view version changes on the `/article/<article_id>/versions` page.\n\n### 3. Approval Workflow\n\n- Approvals are recorded in `approvals.txt` referencing article and version.\n- Approval entries include status (approved, rejected, revision_requested), approver comments, and timestamp.\n- The workflow stages from `workflow_stages.txt` define mandatory reviews per category.\n- Services orchestrate moving articles through approval stages accordingly.\n\n### 4. Comments on Versions\n\n- Comments made by users on specific versions are saved in `comments.txt`.\n- Comments include comment text, author, timestamp, and link to version and article.\n\n### 5. Storage Interaction\n\n- On article version save, a new record appends to `article_versions.txt`.\n- Approval submissions append records to `approvals.txt`.\n- Comments saved by appending to `comments.txt`.\n- Version and approval lookup uses corresponding models parsing these files.\n\n---\n\n## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points\n\n### 1. Data Passing to Frontend Templates\n\n- Controllers pass data as context variables to templates using Flask's `render_template()`.\n- Context variable keys correspond to those listed per route in design_spec.md to ensure consistent frontend data binding.\n- E.g., `dashboard()` passes `username`, `quick_stats`, `recent_activity` variables.\n\n### 2. Endpoint Responses\n\n- Most routes respond to GET requests by rendering templates with populated context.\n- POST routes handle form submissions and return the same template with success/error messages in context for display by frontend.\n- For dynamic pages with data filtering or state change (e.g., calendar POST), updated context is passed for re-render.\n\n### 3. Coordination Points with Frontend Team\n\n- Frontend expects specific data structures:\n  - Lists of dicts for articles and versions with specific keys matching data fields.\n  - Dictionary structures for analytics and quick stats.\n  - Strings or enums for filters and status values.\n- Naming conventions of context variables must be consistent.\n- Pagination, sorting, and filtering parameters passed from frontend must be supported in backend (via query params or POST forms).\n- Backend must handle validation and provide meaningful error messages to be rendered by frontend UI elements.\n\n---\n\nThis architecture.md serves as the definitive guide enabling backend and frontend teams to develop ContentPublishingHub independently yet consistently following this design blueprint.\n\n\n"})
